<div id="review_24160457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24160457" />
    <a title="Imogen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33887-imogen"><img alt="Imogen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353870889p2/33887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24160457?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Imogen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Imogen" href="/user/show/33887-imogen">Imogen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24160457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15520820114198962156">When I am not reading David Sedaris, I am thinking: David Sedaris, man, there is a popular guy whose books are kind of just always around and not very interesting. But when I *am* reading him, I'm always like, there are five or six absolutely brilliant punchlines in every one of this guy's books, and the other parts are, y'know, enjoyable enough. <br/><br/>I think it's a testament to my always forgetting how much I like him that I guess I've read all his stuff, but I absolutely never think of him as an au</span>
  <span id="freeText15520820114198962156" style="display:none">When I am not reading David Sedaris, I am thinking: David Sedaris, man, there is a popular guy whose books are kind of just always around and not very interesting. But when I *am* reading him, I'm always like, there are five or six absolutely brilliant punchlines in every one of this guy's books, and the other parts are, y'know, enjoyable enough. <br /><br />I think it's a testament to my always forgetting how much I like him that I guess I've read all his stuff, but I absolutely never think of him as an author I like when I'm thinking about authors I like. <br /><br />I definitely appreciate that he's a big homo- there's a point in this book where he says that something he's eating tastes kind of like penis- who absolutely kills the Barnes &amp; Noble circuit. Kind of like Chuck Palahniuk, except more explicit. <br /><br />I also like that one time at the Strand he was reading and he asked, 'who here is totally stoked about the new George Romero zombie movie?' and I was all WOOOOOO and the whole rest of the room was silent, so we had a moment. That was good. <br /><br />Anyway, I don't know if I'd pay twenty-five dollars for this as a new book, but I don't know if I'd pay twenty-five dollars for anything as a new book, so that is the wrong question to ask me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15520820114198962156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_29997855" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29997855" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1421547-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307912757p2/1421547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29997855?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/1421547-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29997855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4899846133565651293">Some people find that after reading one or two of Sedaris's books, he becomes less ha-ha funny. Maybe they get used to his style of humour. Maybe there's a golden order in which to read them (personally, I find chronologically by publishing date works well). Maybe there is a slight advantage to hearing him speak in person. I tend to read him while imagining how he'd say it, and immediately a dry sentence comes to life.<br/><br/>I could go on about the maturation I see happening in his work, but I won't. N</span>
  <span id="freeText4899846133565651293" style="display:none">Some people find that after reading one or two of Sedaris's books, he becomes less ha-ha funny. Maybe they get used to his style of humour. Maybe there's a golden order in which to read them (personally, I find chronologically by publishing date works well). Maybe there is a slight advantage to hearing him speak in person. I tend to read him while imagining how he'd say it, and immediately a dry sentence comes to life.<br /><br />I could go on about the maturation I see happening in his work, but I won't. Not for now.<br /><br />What I will say is that in his past work, he seems to be a sort of bystander in many of his stories. Things happen around him. He observes. Takes notes. Then turns them into stories. But rarely is he at the center of the story - the obvious exception being "Me Talk Pretty One Day."<br /><br />This book is different. This is a collection of mostly unrelated stories, and his presence in all of them is more noticeable. More nostalgia, and a dark softness pervades these stories. I really appreciate this quality.<br /><br />Plus, he gets brownie points in my book for using Van Gogh on the cover :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4899846133565651293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KduJiocGWezUbdLnUyqHrOv2EfqsNiiqhSKEjtJ3fJW5TiLG1lpYaZl4lXfVrbrBrWo9+O+JXn2K5xYrtbB9Fw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('01wIE3bVv0NIJzVGSHtDdnpBErhNhqa656WWIptwC/5DyaNfJ4m+xgUyctbO/H4bPN0+ug450G3oYASH/LcKfA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2849.David_Sedaris">About David Sedaris</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2849.David_Sedaris"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1213737698p3/2849.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2849.David_Sedaris">David Sedaris
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16975637346289753398"><b>David Sedaris</b> is a Grammy Award-nominated American humorist and radio contributor.<br/><br/>Sedaris came to prominence in 1992 when National Public Radio broadcast his essay "SantaLand Diaries." He published his first collection of essays and short stories, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4143.Barrel_Fever' title='Barrel Fever' rel='nofollow noopener'>Barrel Fever</a>, in 1994. Each of his four subsequent essay collections, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4138.Naked' title='Naked' rel='nofollow noopener'>Naked</a> (1997), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4136.Holidays_on_Ice' title='Holidays on Ice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holidays on Ice</a> (1997), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4137.Me_Talk_Pretty_One_Day' title='Me Talk Pretty One Day' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Talk Pretty One Day</a> (2000), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10176.Dress_Your_Family_in_Corduroy_and_Denim' title='Dress Your Family in Corduroy and Denim' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dress Your Fa</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16975637346289753398" style="display:none"><b>David Sedaris</b> is a Grammy Award-nominated American humorist and radio contributor.<br /><br />Sedaris came to prominence in 1992 when National Public Radio broadcast his essay "SantaLand Diaries." He published his first collection of essays and short stories, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4143.Barrel_Fever" title="Barrel Fever" rel="nofollow noopener">Barrel Fever</a>, in 1994. Each of his four subsequent essay collections, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4138.Naked" title="Naked" rel="nofollow noopener">Naked</a> (1997), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4136.Holidays_on_Ice" title="Holidays on Ice" rel="nofollow noopener">Holidays on Ice</a> (1997), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4137.Me_Talk_Pretty_One_Day" title="Me Talk Pretty One Day" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Talk Pretty One Day</a> (2000), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10176.Dress_Your_Family_in_Corduroy_and_Denim" title="Dress Your Family in Corduroy and Denim" rel="nofollow noopener">Dress Your Family in Corduroy and Denim</a> (2004), and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1044355.When_You_Are_Engulfed_in_Flames" title="When You Are Engulfed in Flames" rel="nofollow noopener">When You Are Engulfed in Flames</a> (2008) have become New York Times Best Sellers.<br /><br />As of 2008, his books have collectively sold seven million copies. Much of Sedaris' humor is autobiographical and self-deprecating, and it often concerns his family life, his middle class upbringing in the suburbs of Raleigh, North Carolina, Greek heritage, various jobs, education, drug use, homosexuality, and his life in France with his partner, Hugh Hamrick.<br /><br /><i>Excerpted from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Sedaris" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16975637346289753398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
